Now, compute p_x = (1+R-r)/2. But R and r are not independent; they are related by the fact that the circles intersect. We can also express R in terms of x0,y0: R^2 = (x0-1)^2+y0^2 = r^2 -2x0+1. So R = sqrt(r^2 -2x0+1). That's messy.

Maybe we can avoid explicit r and R by using the fact that the line through M and P? Not.

Another approach: Use coordinate geometry with the line MN as x-axis, and set the coordinates such that the intersection points are A=(x0,y0), B=(x0,-y0). Then we can compute everything in terms of x0,y0 and d=1? Actually, we have d=1 by scaling. So we have x0 = (1+r^2-R^2)/2. But we also have r^2 = x0^2+y0^2. So x0 = (1+(x0^2+y0^2) - R^2)/2 => 2x0 = 1 + x0^2+y0^2 - R^2 => R^2 = 1 + x0^2+y0^2 - 2x0 = (x0-1)^2+y0^2, which is consistent. So we can use x0,y0 as parameters. Then r^2 = x0^2+y0^2, R^2 = (x0-1)^2+y0^2. So r = sqrt(x0^2+y0^2), R = sqrt((x0-1)^2+y0^2). Then p_x = (1+R-r)/2, p_y = - (x0+r) p_x / y0. Then H = (p_x, - y0 (1-p_x)/(x0+r)). And w = (1, - (r+x0)/y0). So the line L_H is through H with direction w.

Now, compute t_E and t_F. But note that v = P-A = (p_x-x0, p_y-y0). We have p_x-x0 = (1+R-r)/2 - x0. Using R^2 = (x0-1)^2+y0^2, we can compute (1+R-r)/2 - x0. This is messy. However, we can compute A·v and (A-n)·v. Since v is proportional to w, we have v = k w for some k. Indeed, we earlier found that v = (v_x, - (r+x0) v_x / y0) = v_x (1, - (r+x0)/y0) = v_x w. So v = v_x w. So A·v = v_x (A·w). And A·w = x0*1 + y0*(- (r+x0)/y0) = x0 - (r+x0) = -r. So A·w = -r. Thus A·v = -r v_x. So t_E = -2 A·v/|v|^2 = -2 (-r v_x)/ (v_x^2 |w|^2) = 2r/(v_x |w|^2). Similarly, (A-n)·w =? A-n = (x0-1, y0). So (A-n)·w = (x0-1)*1 + y0*(- (r+x0)/y0) = x0-1 - (r+x0) = -r -1. So (A-n)·w = -(r+1). Then (A-n)·v = v_x (A-n)·w = -v_x (r+1). So t_F = -2 (A-n)·v/|v|^2 = -2 (-v_x (r+1))/ (v_x^2 |w|^2) = 2(r+1)/(v_x |w|^2).

Thus t_E = 2r/(v_x |w|^2), t_F = 2(r+1)/(v_x |w|^2). So t_F = t_E * (r+1)/r. So t_F > t_E, consistent.

Now, we also have v_x = p_x - x0 = (1+R-r)/2 - x0. But we can compute v_x in terms of x0,y0? Since R = sqrt((x0-1)^2+y0^2). Not nice. But we can also compute |w|^2 = 1 + ((r+x0)/y0)^2 = (y0^2 + (r+x0)^2)/y0^2 = ( (x0^2+y0^2) + (r+x0)^2? Wait, y0^2 + (r+x0)^2 = y0^2 + r^2 + 2r x0 + x0^2 = (x0^2+y0^2) + r^2 + 2r x0 = r^2 + r^2 + 2r x0 = 2r^2 + 2r x0 = 2r(r+x0). So |w|^2 = 2r(r+x0)/y0^2.

Thus |w|^2 = 2r(r+x0)/y0^2.

Now, t_E = 2r/(v_x |w|^2) = 2r/(v_x * 2r(r+x0)/y0^2) = y0^2/(v_x (r+x0)). So t_E = y0^2/( (r+x0) v_x ). Similarly, t_F = 2(r+1)/(v_x |w|^2) = 2(r+1)/(v_x * 2r(r+x0)/y0^2) = (r+1) y0^2/( r (r+x0) v_x ). So t_F = t_E * (r+1)/r. Good.

Now, we also have v_x = (1+R-r)/2 - x0. But we can express R in terms of x0,y0? R = sqrt((x0-1)^2+y0^2). So v_x is not simple. However, we can also compute p_x = (1+R-r)/2. And we have p_x = x0 + v_x. So v_x = p_x - x0.

Now, we have H = (p_x, - y0 (1-p_x)/(x0+r)). Also, w = (1, - (r+x0)/y0). So line L_H: (x,y) = (p_x, - y0 (1-p_x)/(x0+r)) + s (1, - (r+x0)/y0). So its equation: y - y_H = m (x - x_H) where m = - (r+x0)/y0. So y = - (r+x0)/y0 x + c, with c = y_H + m x_H = - y0 (1-p_x)/(x0+r) + ( - (r+x0)/y0 ) p_x = - y0 (1-p_x)/(x0+r) - p_x (r+x0)/y0.

Now, points: B = (x0, -y0). E = A + α w, where α = t_E v_x? Actually, we have E = A + t_E v, and v = v_x w, so E = A + t_E v_x w. So α = t_E v_x = y0^2/( (r+x0) v_x ) * v_x = y0^2/(r+x0). So α = y0^2/(r+x0). Similarly, β = t_F v_x = (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0) v_x) * v_x = (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)). So β = (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)). Thus E = A + α w, F = A + β w.

Now, A = (x0, y0), w = (1, - (r+x0)/y0). So we can compute E and F coordinates.

E = (x0 + α, y0 - α (r+x0)/y0) = (x0 + y0^2/(r+x0), y0 - (y0^2/(r+x0)) * (r+x0)/y0) = (x0 + y0^2/(r+x0), y0 - y0) = (x0 + y0^2/(r+x0), 0). So E lies on the x-axis! That's nice: E = (x0 + y0^2/(r+x0), 0). Similarly, F = (x0 + β, y0 - β (r+x0)/y0) = (x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), y0 - ((r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0))) * (r+x0)/y0) = (x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), y0 - (r+1) y0/r) = (x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), y0 (1 - (r+1)/r) ) = (x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), y0 ( (r - r -1)/r ) ) = (x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), - y0/r ). So F = (X_F, Y_F) with X_F = x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)), Y_F = - y0/r.

Thus we have:

- B = (x0, -y0)
- E = (e_x, 0) where e_x = x0 + y0^2/(r+x0)
- F = (f_x, -y0/r)

Now, note that E is on the x-axis. So triangle BEF has vertices B, E on x-axis, and F above or below? Since y0>0, -y0/r is negative (r>0), so F is below x-axis. So all three points are on or below x-axis? B has y=-y0<0, E has y=0, F has y=-y0/r<0. So triangle BEF is not degenerate.

Now, we want to show that line L_H (through H with slope - (r+x0)/y0) is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF. We can compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF using the formula for three points. Since E is on x-axis, and B and F have y-coordinates, we can find the perpendicular bisector of BE and BF. Let's do that.

Let’s denote:

- x0, y0 >0, r = sqrt(x0^2+y0^2) >0.
- e_x = x0 + y0^2/(r+x0). Since r+x0 >0, e_x > x0.
- f_x = x0 + (r+1) y0^2/(r (r+x0)).
- Y_F = - y0/r.

Now, B = (x0, -y0). E = (e_x, 0). F = (f_x, -y0/r). We can compute the circumcenter O.

The perpendicular bisector of BE: midpoint M_BE = ((x0+e_x)/2, (-y0+0)/2) = ((x0+e_x)/2, -y0/2). Slope of BE: (0 - (-y0))/(e_x - x0) = y0/(e_x - x0). So perpendicular slope = - (e_x - x0)/y0. Thus equation: y + y0/2 = - (e_x - x0)/y0 (x - (x0+e_x)/2). (Equation 1)

Perpendicular bisector of BF: midpoint M_BF = ((x0+f_x)/2, (-y0 + (-y0/r))/2 = ((x0+f_x)/2, -y0(1+1/r)/2). Slope of BF: ( -y0/r - (-y0) )/(f_x - x0) = ( -y0/r + y0 )/(f_x - x0) = y0(1 - 1/r)/(f_x - x0). So perpendicular slope = - (f_x - x0)/( y0(1 - 1/r) ) = - (f_x - x0)/( y0 * ( (r-1)/r ) ) = - r (f_x - x0)/( y0 (r-1) ). Equation: y + y0(1+1/r)/2 = - r (f_x - x0)/( y0 (r-1) ) ( x - (x0+f_x)/2 ). (Equation 2)
